<file path="src/content/docs/en/guide/tool-calling.mdx">
---
title: Tool Calling and Dispatch
description: How MCP and WebMCP tools are called, routed, and executed
sidebar:
  order: 3
---

**Tool calling** is the core of WebMCP Auto-UI. The LLM agent requests tools, and the dispatcher routes them to the correct server (MCP or WebMCP).

## Anatomy of a Tool Call

### 1. Agent generates a tool_use block

```typescript
// LLM response
{
  type: 'tool_use',
  id: 'toolu_1234',
  name: 'weather_mcp_get_forecast',
  input: { location: 'Paris', days: 3 }
}
```

### 2. Dispatcher routes the call

```typescript
// In runAgentLoop, dispatcher.ts processes each block
for (const block of toolBlocks) {
  // Resolve alias
  const resolvedName = aliasMap.get(block.name) ?? block.name;
  
  // Parse prefix: {serverName}_{protocol}_{toolName}
  const match = resolvedName.match(/^(.+?)_(mcp|webmcp)_(.+)$/);
  if (!match) {
    // Error: invalid format
    result = `Error: unknown tool format`;
  } else {
    const [, serverName, protocol, realToolName] = match;
    
    // Routing
    if (protocol === 'mcp') {
      // → MCP client.callTool()
    } else if (protocol === 'webmcp') {
      // → WebMCP server.executeTool()
    }
  }
}
```

### 3. Interceptor (pseudo-tools)

Before normal dispatch, two **pseudo-tools** are intercepted locally:

```typescript
// list_tools, search_tools — no server activation
if (toolMatch && (toolMatch[3] === 'list_tools' || toolMatch[3] === 'search_tools')) {
  const layer = layers.find(l => 
    sanitizeServerName(l.serverName) === serverName && 
    l.protocol === protocol
  );
  
  // Return the list without touching the server
  if (pseudoTool === 'list_tools') {
    result = JSON.stringify(layer.tools);
  } else {
    // search_tools
    const query = String(block.input.query ?? '').toLowerCase();
    const matches = layer.tools.filter(t =>
      t.name.toLowerCase().includes(query) ||
      t.description.toLowerCase().includes(query)
    );
    result = JSON.stringify(matches);
  }
}
```

### 4. Lazy server activation

On **first call** to a server tool:

```typescript
const activateMatch = block.name.match(/^(.+?)_(mcp|webmcp)_(.+)$/);
if (activateMatch) {
  const [, serverName, protocol] = activateMatch;
  const serverKey = `${serverName}_${protocol}`;
  
  if (!activatedServers.has(serverKey)) {
    activatedServers.add(serverKey);
    const layer = layers.find(l => 
      sanitizeServerName(l.serverName) === serverName && 
      l.protocol === protocol
    );
    if (layer) {
      // Add ALL server tools to activeTools
      activeTools = activateServerTools(activeTools, layer);
    }
  }
}
```

## MCP Dispatch

```mermaid
graph LR
    A["tool_use block\n{name: server_mcp_tool}"] -->|parse| B["name match\n+ resolveAlias"]
    B -->|MCP branch| C["McpClient\n.callTool()"]
    C -->|HTTP/SSE| D["MCP Server\n(network)"]
    D -->|result JSON| E["Compress\nif > 300 chars"]
    E -->|tool_result| F["Messages\nfor agent"]
```

### MCP Code

```typescript
if (protocol === 'mcp') {
  if (!client) {
    result = `Error: no MCP client available for tool ${name}`;
  } else {
    const mcpResult = await client.callTool(realToolName, block.input);
    const textContent = mcpResult.content?.find(
      (c) => c.type === 'text'
    ) as { text?: string } | undefined;
    const rawResult = textContent?.text ?? JSON.stringify(mcpResult);
    
    // Truncate if result > 10,000 chars (default MAX_RESULT_LEN)
    result = truncateResults 
      ? truncateResult(rawResult, maxResultLength) 
      : rawResult;
  }
}
```

**Network**: The MCP client establishes an SSE (Server-Sent Events) connection to the remote server and calls `tools/call`.

## WebMCP Dispatch

```mermaid
graph LR
    A["tool_use block\n{name: server_webmcp_tool}"] -->|parse| B["name match\n+ resolveAlias"]
    B -->|WebMCP branch| C{"Tool name?"}
    C -->|recall| D["Check resultBuffer\n+ return full"]
    C -->|widget_display| E["Validate schema\n+ sanitize URLs"]
    C -->|canvas| F["Route to callbacks\n(onMove, onResize, etc)"]
    C -->|other| G["WebMCP server\n.executeTool()"]
    D -->|string| H["tool_result"]
    E -->|{widget,data,id}| H
    F -->|{ok:true}| H
    G -->|result| H
```

### WebMCP Code

```typescript
if (protocol === 'webmcp') {
  // ── Special: recall (re-read a compressed result) ──
  if (realToolName === 'recall' && resultBuffer.size > 0) {
    const recallId = (block.input as { id: string }).id;
    result = resultBuffer.get(recallId) 
      ?? `No result found for id '${recallId}'.`;
  } else {
    // ── Normal dispatch to WebMCP server ──
    const webmcpServer = webmcpServers.get(serverName);
    if (!webmcpServer) {
      result = `Error: no WebMCP server "${serverName}" found.`;
    } else {
      const toolResult = await webmcpServer.executeTool(
        realToolName, 
        block.input
      );
      result = typeof toolResult === 'string' 
        ? toolResult 
        : JSON.stringify(toolResult);
      
      // ── Special: widget_display ──
      if (realToolName === 'widget_display') {
        const wr = toolResult as Record<string, unknown>;
        if (wr.widget && wr.data && !wr.error) {
          const widgetResult = callbacks.onWidget?.(
            wr.widget as string, 
            wr.data as Record<string, unknown>
          );
          if (widgetResult?.id) {
            result = JSON.stringify({ ...wr, id: widgetResult.id });
          }
        }
      }
      
      // ── Special: canvas (UI actions) ──
      if (realToolName === 'canvas') {
        const action = block.input.action as string;
        const id = block.input.id as string;
        const actionParams = block.input.params as Record<string, unknown>;
        
        switch (action) {
          case 'clear': callbacks.onClear?.(); break;
          case 'update': callbacks.onUpdate?.(id, actionParams ?? {}); break;
          case 'move': callbacks.onMove?.(
            id, 
            (actionParams?.x ?? block.input.x) as number,
            (actionParams?.y ?? block.input.y) as number
          ); break;
          case 'resize': callbacks.onResize?.(
            id,
            (actionParams?.width ?? block.input.width) as number,
            (actionParams?.height ?? block.input.height) as number
          ); break;
          case 'style': callbacks.onStyle?.(
            id,
            (actionParams?.styles ?? block.input.styles) as Record<string, string>
          ); break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

## Widget Display (special case)

`widget_display()` is the main tool for **UI rendering**:

```mermaid
graph LR
    A["widget_display\n(name, params)"] -->|validate| B["Get widget schema\nfrom autoui"]
    B -->|JSON Schema| C["validateJsonSchema\n(params)"]
    C -->|valid| D["sanitizeImageUrls\n(params)"]
    D -->|cleaned| E["Generate widget ID\nw_xxxxx"]
    E -->|{widget,data,id}| F["onWidget callback"]
    F -->|Canvas.addWidget| G["Store widget"]
    G -->|$state reactivity| H["WidgetRenderer\nmounts component"]
    
    C -->|invalid| I["Return errors\n+ expected schema"]
    I -->|agent retry| A
```

### Complete Example

```typescript
// Agent calls
{
  type: 'tool_use',
  id: 'toolu_5678',
  name: 'autoui_webmcp_widget_display',
  input: {
    name: 'stat-card',
    params: {
      label: 'Conversion',
      value: '3.2%',
      unit: '%',
      trend: 'up',
      variant: 'success'
    }
  }
}

// Dispatcher:
// 1. Get schema for 'stat-card' widget
// 2. Validate params vs schema
// 3. Sanitize image URLs (none to remove here)
// 4. Generate ID 'w_1a2b3c'
// 5. Call onWidget('stat-card', {...params})
// 6. Canvas adds widget: { id: 'w_1a2b3c', type: 'stat-card', data: {...} }
// 7. WidgetRenderer mounts StatCard component with props
// 8. UI displays the card
```

## Canvas Tools (UI manipulation)

The `canvas` tool allows the agent to **rearrange widgets**:

```typescript
// Agent calls
{
  type: 'tool_use',
  name: 'autoui_webmcp_canvas',
  input: {
    action: 'move',
    id: 'w_1a2b3c',
    params: { x: 100, y: 50 }
  }
}

// Callbacks in agent
callbacks.onMove?.('w_1a2b3c', 100, 50);
// → Update CSS widget position
```

**Actions**:
- `clear()` — empty canvas
- `update(id, data)` — modify widget data
- `move(id, x, y)` — reposition (CSS transform)
- `resize(id, width, height)` — resize
- `style(id, styles)` — apply CSS styles

## Recall (re-read compressed results)

After ~2 iterations, **old tool results** are compressed to save context:

```typescript
// Before compression
{
  type: 'tool_result',
  tool_use_id: 'toolu_1234',
  content: '{"data": [item1, item2, ... item1000], "total": 1000}'
}

// After compression (mutated in-place)
{
  type: 'tool_result',
  tool_use_id: 'toolu_1234',
  content: '{"data": [item1, item2, ... [recall(\'toolu_1234\') for complete result, 5000 chars]'
}

// Stored in resultBuffer
resultBuffer.set('toolu_1234', '{"data": [item1, item2, ... item1000], "total": 1000}');
```

If the agent calls `recall('toolu_1234')`:

```typescript
// Dispatcher intercepts recall
if (realToolName === 'recall' && resultBuffer.size > 0) {
  const recallId = (block.input as { id: string }).id;
  result = resultBuffer.get(recallId) ?? `No result found...`;
}
```

**Advantage**: Agent can navigate multiple data layers without blocking context.

## Error Handling

### Schema validation error

```typescript
// Invalid widget params
{
  type: 'tool_use',
  name: 'autoui_webmcp_widget_display',
  input: {
    name: 'stat',
    params: { label: 'Sales' }  // ✗ missing value
  }
}

// Response
{
  type: 'tool_result',
  content: JSON.stringify({
    error: 'Validation failed',
    details: [{ path: '/value', message: 'required' }],
    expected_schema: { ... }
  })
}

// Agent receives error + schema → retries with correct fields
```

### Tool not found

```typescript
// MCP
if (!client) {
  result = `Error: no MCP client available for tool ${name}`;
}

// WebMCP
if (!webmcpServer) {
  result = `Error: no WebMCP server "${serverName}" found.`;
}
```

### Tool execution failure

```typescript
try {
  const toolResult = await webmcpServer.executeTool(realToolName, block.input);
  result = ...;
} catch (e) {
  call.error = e instanceof Error ? e.message : String(e);
  toolResults.push({ 
    type: 'tool_result', 
    tool_use_id: block.id, 
    content: `Error: ${call.error}` 
  });
}
```

## Metrics and Monitoring

Each tool call is tracked:

```typescript
const call: ToolCall = {
  id: block.id,
  name: block.name,
  args: block.input,
  result: result,
  error: undefined,
  elapsed: Math.round(performance.now() - t1),
  guided: wasDiscovering,  // true if preceded by discovery tool
};

metrics.toolCalls++;
callbacks.onToolCall?.(call);  // subscriber can log
```

**Useful for**: analytics, debugging, agent optimization.

## Flow Summary

1. **LLM generates** `tool_use` block
2. **Dispatcher detects** format + resolves alias
3. **Pseudo-tools** (list_tools, search_tools) → local response
4. **Lazy activation**: if 1st call, add all server tools
5. **Routing**: MCP → network, WebMCP → local
6. **Post-processing**: compression, sanitize, callbacks
7. **tool_result** returns to agent
8. **Next iteration** of loop
</file>

<file path="src/content/docs/en/packages/agent.mdx">
---
title: "@webmcp-auto-ui/agent"
description: "LLM agent with MCP/WebMCP support, multiple providers, tool layers, and recipe execution."
sidebar:
  order: 1
---

The `@webmcp-auto-ui/agent` package provides complete orchestration for executing an LLM agent loop with MCP (Model Context Protocol) and WebMCP support, tool management, lazy loading, and recipe execution.

## Main Exports

### runAgentLoop

Executes an LLM agent loop → tool call → LLM until `end_turn` or `max_iterations`.

```ts
import { runAgentLoop } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const result = await runAgentLoop(userMessage, {
  provider: remoteLLMProvider,
  layers: toolLayers,
  maxIterations: 5,
  callbacks: {
    onToken: (token) => console.log(token),
    onToolCall: (call) => console.log('Tool:', call.name),
  },
});

// result: AgentResult
// - text: final text response
// - toolCalls: array of all tool calls
// - metrics: tokens, latency, iterations
// - messages: complete conversation history
// - stopReason: 'end_turn' | 'max_iterations'
```

**Interface AgentLoopOptions:**

```ts
interface AgentLoopOptions {
  client?: McpClient;              // MCP client (optional if WebMCP only)
  provider: LLMProvider;           // LLM provider (required)
  layers?: ToolLayer[];            // Structured tool layers
  maxIterations?: number;          // Max iterations (default: 5)
  maxTokens?: number;              // Max output tokens
  maxTools?: number;               // Max tools per LLM call
  temperature?: number;            // LLM temperature
  topK?: number;                   // Top K sampling
  cacheEnabled?: boolean;          // Prompt cache (default: true)
  systemPrompt?: string;           // Custom system prompt
  initialMessages?: ChatMessage[]; // Previous history
  callbacks?: AgentCallbacks;      // Streaming callbacks
  signal?: AbortSignal;            // Cancellation
  truncateResults?: boolean;       // Truncate results (default: true)
  compressHistory?: boolean;       // Compress old results (default: true)
  maxResultLength?: number;        // Max result chars (default: 10000)
}
```

**Interface AgentResult:**

```ts
interface AgentResult {
  text: string;
  toolCalls: ToolCall[];
  metrics: AgentMetrics;
  stopReason: 'end_turn' | 'max_iterations';
  messages: ChatMessage[];  // Complete conversation
}
```

**Available Callbacks:**

```ts
interface AgentCallbacks {
  onIterationStart?: (iteration: number, maxIterations: number) => void;
  onLLMRequest?: (messages: ChatMessage[], tools: ProviderTool[]) => void;
  onLLMResponse?: (response: LLMResponse, latencyMs: number, tokens?: { input: number; output: number }) => void;
  onToolCall?: (call: ToolCall) => void;
  onWidget?: (type: string, data: Record<string, unknown>) => { id: string } | void;
  onClear?: () => void;
  onText?: (text: string) => void;
  onToken?: (token: string) => void;
  onDone?: (metrics: AgentMetrics) => void;
  onUpdate?: (id: string, data: Record<string, unknown>) => void;
  onMove?: (id: string, x: number, y: number) => void;
  onResize?: (id: string, w: number, h: number) => void;
  onStyle?: (id: string, styles: Record<string, string>) => void;
}
```

### LLM Providers

#### RemoteLLMProvider

Anthropic Claude provider (via remote API).

```ts
import { RemoteLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const provider = new RemoteLLMProvider({
  proxyUrl: '/api/chat',
  model: 'sonnet',  // resolves to claude-sonnet-4-6
});
```

**Options:**

```ts
interface RemoteLLMProviderOptions {
  proxyUrl: string;
  model?: string;  // 'haiku' | 'sonnet' | 'opus' (default: 'haiku')
  apiKey?: string;  // injected in body, read by proxy +server.ts
}
```

#### WasmProvider

Gemma 2 provider (in-browser, via WASM with Web Workers).

```ts
import { WasmProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const provider = new WasmProvider({
  modelSize: '2b',  // '2b' or '7b'
  quantized: true,  // Quantized 4-bit (recommended)
  workerUrl: new URL('@webmcp-auto-ui/agent/gemma-worker', import.meta.url),
});

// Wait for loading
await provider.ready();
```

**Status Events:**

```ts
interface WasmStatus {
  type: 'initializing' | 'loading' | 'ready' | 'error';
  progress?: number;       // 0-1
  message?: string;
}

provider.onStatus((status) => {
  console.log(status.type, status.progress);
});
```

#### LocalLLMProvider

Ollama provider (local LLM via server).

```ts
import { LocalLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const provider = new LocalLLMProvider({
  baseUrl: 'http://localhost:11434',
  model: 'mistral',
});
```

### Tool Layers

**Tool layers** structure MCP/WebMCP tools in layers for lazy loading and system prompt injection.

```ts
export type ToolLayer = McpLayer | WebMcpLayer;

interface McpLayer {
  protocol: 'mcp';
  serverName: string;
  description?: string;
  tools: McpToolDef[];
  recipes?: McpRecipe[];
}

interface WebMcpLayer {
  protocol: 'webmcp';
  serverName: string;
  description: string;
  tools: WebMcpToolDef[];
}
```

#### buildSystemPromptWithAliases

Generate system prompt with tool aliases (for MCP canonical matching).

```ts
import { buildSystemPromptWithAliases } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const { prompt, aliasMap } = buildSystemPromptWithAliases(layers);

// prompt: complete system text
// aliasMap: Map<"alias_name", "real_name"> for dynamic resolution
```

The prompt includes execution steps and discovery pseudo-tools (`search_tools`, `list_tools`).

#### buildDiscoveryToolsWithAliases

Build the initial list of discovery tools (before server activation).

```ts
import { buildDiscoveryToolsWithAliases } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const { tools, aliasMap } = buildDiscoveryToolsWithAliases(layers);

// tools: ProviderTool[] (discovery + alias)
// aliasMap: Map for resolution
```

#### activateServerTools

Activate all tools of a layer (lazy loading on first contact).

```ts
import { activateServerTools } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const nextTools = activateServerTools(currentTools, layer);
```

#### resolveCanonicalTools

Resolve MCP tools to canonical roles (search_recipes, list_recipes, get_recipe) via 4 matching layers.

```ts
import { resolveCanonicalTools } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const matches = resolveCanonicalTools(mcpTools);

// matches: CanonicalMatch[]
// - role: 'search_recipes' | 'list_recipes' | 'get_recipe'
// - realToolName: real MCP tool name
```

The 4 layers:
1. **Exact match** — search `search_recipes`, `list_recipes`, `get_recipe`
2. **Decompose** — tokenize name and test all pairs (action, resource)
3. **Description keywords** — scan description for recipe/template/workflow
4. **Fallback** — no match

### Type Definitions

```ts
interface ToolCall {
  id: string;
  name: string;
  args: Record<string, unknown>;
  result?: string;
  error?: string;
  elapsed?: number;
  guided?: boolean;  // Preceded by discovery tool
}

interface AgentMetrics {
  totalTokens: number;
  promptTokens: number;
  completionTokens: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
  toolCalls: number;
  iterations: number;
  cacheHits: number;
}

interface ChatMessage {
  role: 'user' | 'assistant' | 'system';
  content: string | ContentBlock[];
}

type ContentBlock =
  | { type: 'text'; text: string }
  | { type: 'tool_use'; id: string; name: string; input: Record<string, unknown> }
  | { type: 'tool_result'; tool_use_id: string; content: string };

interface LLMResponse {
  content: ContentBlock[];
  stopReason: string;
  usage?: { input_tokens: number; output_tokens: number; cache_read_input_tokens?: number };
}
```

## Built-in WebMCP Server (autoui)

```ts
import { autoui, NATIVE_WIDGET_NAMES } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

// autoui: WebMcpServer with all native widgets pre-registered
// - stat, kv, list, chart, alert, code, text, actions, tags
// - stat-card, data-table, timeline, profile, trombinoscope
// - json-viewer, hemicycle, chart-rich, cards, grid-data
// - sankey, map, log, gallery, carousel, d3, js-sandbox
// - recipe-browser (special widget view)

// Plus native tools:
// - widget_display(name, params) — display a widget
// - canvas(action, id, params) — manipulate canvas (clear, update, move, resize, style)
// - recall(id) — replay complete result (from buffer)
// - search_recipes(query) — search by keyword
// - list_recipes() — list all widgets
// - get_recipe(name) — get widget details
```

## Token Tracker

Track tokens and latency in real time.

```ts
import { TokenTracker } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const tracker = new TokenTracker();

tracker.track('prompt', 100);     // Input tokens
tracker.track('completion', 50);  // Output tokens
tracker.track('latency', 1200);   // Latency in ms

const metrics = tracker.getMetrics();
// {
//   totalTokens: 150,
//   promptTokens: 100,
//   completionTokens: 50,
//   totalLatencyMs: 1200,
//   tokensPerSec: 0.125
// }
```

## Utilities

### toProviderTools

Convert `McpToolDef[]` to `ProviderTool[]` (Anthropic format).

```ts
import { toProviderTools } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const providerTools = toProviderTools(mcpTools);
```

### fromMcpTools

Convert `McpTool[]` (from core) to `McpToolDef[]` (agent).

```ts
import { fromMcpTools } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const toolDefs = fromMcpTools(tools);
```

### trimConversationHistory

Reduce history to a token budget by removing oldest messages.

```ts
import { trimConversationHistory } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const trimmed = trimConversationHistory(messages, 4096);
```

## Complete Example

```ts
import { runAgentLoop, RemoteLLMProvider, autoui } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

// 1. Create an LLM provider
const provider = new RemoteLLMProvider({
  proxyUrl: '/api/chat',
  model: 'sonnet',  // resolves to claude-sonnet-4-6
});

// 2. Create an MCP client (if connecting to MCP servers)
const client = new McpClient('http://localhost:3000/mcp');
await client.initialize();

// 3. Build tool layers
const layers = [
  // MCP Layer
  {
    protocol: 'mcp' as const,
    serverName: 'recipes',
    tools: await client.listTools(),
  },
  // WebMCP Layer (autoui)
  autoui.layer(),
];

// 4. Run agent loop
const result = await runAgentLoop('Display a Q1 sales chart', {
  client,
  provider,
  layers,
  maxIterations: 5,
  callbacks: {
    onToken: (token) => process.stdout.write(token),
    onToolCall: (call) => console.log(`[${call.name}]`),
    onWidget: (type, data) => console.log(`Widget: ${type}`),
  },
});

console.log('Final:', result.text);
console.log('Metrics:', result.metrics);
```
</file>

<file path="src/content/docs/en/packages/core.mdx">
---
title: "@webmcp-auto-ui/core"
description: "Foundations: MCP Client, WebMCP server, JSON schema validation, utilities."
sidebar:
  order: 4
---

The `@webmcp-auto-ui/core` package provides the foundations: MCP client (streamable HTTP), WebMCP server, JSON schema validation, and communication utilities.

## MCP Client

JSON-RPC client for the Model Context Protocol over streamable HTTP.

### McpClient

Class for communicating with an MCP server.

```ts
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const client = new McpClient('http://localhost:3000/mcp', {
  clientName: 'my-app',
  clientVersion: '1.0.0',
  timeout: 30000,
});

// Initialize
await client.initialize();

// List tools
const tools = await client.listTools();
// McpTool[] with name, description, inputSchema

// Call a tool
const result = await client.callTool('search_recipes', {
  query: 'desserts',
});
// McpToolResult { content: [...], isError? }
```

**Options:**

```ts
interface McpClientOptions {
  clientName?: string;              // Default: 'webmcp-client'
  clientVersion?: string;           // Default: '1.0.0'
  timeout?: number;                 // Default: 30000 ms
  headers?: Record<string, string>; // Custom headers
  autoReconnect?: boolean;          // Auto-reconnect
  maxReconnectAttempts?: number;    // Default: 3
}
```

**Methods:**

```ts
client.initialize(): Promise<McpInitializeResult>
client.listTools(): Promise<McpTool[]>
client.callTool(name: string, args: Record<string, unknown>): Promise<McpToolResult>
client.close(): Promise<void>
```

### McpMultiClient

Manage multiple MCP servers in parallel.

```ts
import { McpMultiClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const multi = new McpMultiClient();

await multi.connect('recipes', 'http://localhost:3000/mcp');
await multi.connect('database', 'http://localhost:3001/mcp');

// List connected servers
const servers = multi.listServers();

// Call a tool on a specific server
const result = await multi.callTool('recipes', 'search_recipes', {
  query: 'pasta'
});

// Close all servers
await multi.closeAll();
```

## WebMCP Server

Create a WebMCP server to expose widgets and tools.

### createWebMcpServer

Build a WebMCP server with widgets and tools.

```ts
import { createWebMcpServer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const server = createWebMcpServer('my-widgets', {
  description: 'Custom UI widgets for my app',
});
```

**Register a widget:**

```ts
// Via Markdown recipe with YAML frontmatter
server.registerWidget(`
---
widget: my-chart
description: Custom chart
schema:
  type: object
  properties:
    title:
      type: string
    data:
      type: array
required:
  - data
---

## How to use

Displays a chart with the provided data.
`, renderer);
```

**Vanilla renderer (function):**

```ts
const renderer = (container: HTMLElement, data: Record<string, unknown>) => {
  container.innerHTML = `<h1>${data.title}</h1>`;
  // Optionally return a cleanup function
  return () => {
    // Cleanup if needed
  };
};
```

**Framework renderer (Svelte, React, etc.):**

```ts
// Pass the component directly (non-vanilla)
import MyComponent from './MyComponent.svelte';
server.registerWidget(recipeMd, MyComponent);
```

**Add a custom tool:**

```ts
server.addTool({
  name: 'compute',
  description: 'Perform a computation',
  inputSchema: {
    type: 'object',
    properties: {
      operation: { type: 'string', enum: ['add', 'multiply'] },
      a: { type: 'number' },
      b: { type: 'number' },
    },
    required: ['operation', 'a', 'b'],
  },
  execute: async (params) => {
    const { operation, a, b } = params as { operation: string; a: number; b: number };
    const result = operation === 'add' ? a + b : a * b;
    return { result };
  },
});
```

**List widgets:**

```ts
const widgets = server.listWidgets();
// WidgetEntry[] { name, description, inputSchema, recipe, renderer }

const widget = server.getWidget('my-chart');
if (widget) {
  console.log(widget.description);
  console.log(widget.inputSchema);
}
```

**Export as a layer:**

```ts
const layer = server.layer();
// { protocol: 'webmcp', serverName: 'my-widgets', description: '...', tools: [...] }
```

### parseFrontmatter

Parse the YAML frontmatter from a Markdown recipe.

```ts
import { parseFrontmatter } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const markdown = `---
widget: stat
description: Key statistic
schema:
  type: object
  properties:
    label:
      type: string
    value:
      type: string
---

## When to use
...
`;

const { frontmatter, body } = parseFrontmatter(markdown);
// frontmatter: { widget: 'stat', description: '...', schema: {...} }
// body: '## When to use...'
```

### mountWidget

Mount a vanilla widget into a DOM container.

```ts
import { mountWidget } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const container = document.getElementById('widget');
const cleanup = mountWidget(container, 'stat', {
  label: 'Revenue',
  value: '$42k'
}, [server]);

// Later...
cleanup?.();
```

## JSON Schema Validation

Validate data against a JSON Schema.

### validateJsonSchema

Strictly validate an input against a schema.

```ts
import { validateJsonSchema } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const schema = {
  type: 'object',
  properties: {
    name: { type: 'string' },
    age: { type: 'number', minimum: 0 },
  },
  required: ['name'],
};

const data = { name: 'Alice', age: 30 };
const result = validateJsonSchema(data, schema);

if (!result.valid) {
  console.error(result.errors);
  // ValidationError[] { path, message, expected, actual }
}
```

**Interface:**

```ts
interface ValidationResult {
  valid: boolean;
  errors: ValidationError[];
}

interface ValidationError {
  path: string;           // e.g., '$.properties.age'
  message: string;
  expected?: string;      // e.g., 'number'
  actual?: string;        // e.g., 'string'
}
```

## Utilities

### sanitizeSchema

Clean a JSON schema to make it compatible with the Anthropic API.

```ts
import { sanitizeSchema } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const rawSchema = {
  type: 'object',
  properties: {
    // ...
  },
  // Some fields may not be compatible
};

const clean = sanitizeSchema(rawSchema);
```

Removes:
- Unresolved references (`$ref` without `$defs`)
- Invalid additional properties
- Overly deep nested schemas

### createToolGroup

Create a tool group with a shared namespace.

```ts
import { createToolGroup } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const group = createToolGroup('database', [
  {
    name: 'query',
    description: 'Execute a SQL query',
    inputSchema: { /* ... */ },
  },
  {
    name: 'insert',
    description: 'Insert a record',
    inputSchema: { /* ... */ },
  },
]);

// group.tools:
// - database_query
// - database_insert
```

## Core Types

### JSON Schema

```ts
export type JsonSchemaType =
  | 'string' | 'number' | 'integer' | 'boolean'
  | 'object' | 'array' | 'null';

export interface JsonSchemaObject {
  type?: JsonSchemaType | JsonSchemaType[];
  description?: string;
  properties?: Record<string, JsonSchema>;
  required?: string[];
  items?: JsonSchema | JsonSchema[];
  minLength?: number;
  maxLength?: number;
  minimum?: number;
  maximum?: number;
  enum?: unknown[];
  // ... and more
}

export type JsonSchema = boolean | JsonSchemaObject;
```

### MCP

```ts
export interface McpTool {
  name: string;
  description?: string;
  inputSchema?: JsonSchema;
  outputSchema?: JsonSchema;
}

export interface McpToolResult {
  content: McpToolResultContent[];
  isError?: boolean;
}

export interface McpToolResultContent {
  type: 'text' | 'image' | 'resource';
  text?: string;
  data?: string;
  mimeType?: string;
  resource?: { uri: string; mimeType?: string; text?: string };
}

export interface McpInitializeResult {
  protocolVersion: string;
  capabilities: McpCapabilities;
  serverInfo: McpServerInfo;
}
```

### WebMCP

```ts
export interface WebMcpToolDef {
  name: string;
  description: string;
  inputSchema: Record<string, unknown>;
  execute: (params: Record<string, unknown>) => Promise<unknown>;
}

export interface WidgetEntry {
  name: string;
  description: string;
  inputSchema: Record<string, unknown>;
  recipe: string;
  renderer: WidgetRenderer;
  group?: string;
  vanilla: boolean;
}

export type WidgetRenderer =
  | ((container: HTMLElement, data: Record<string, unknown>) => void | (() => void))
  | unknown;  // Framework component
```

## PostMessage Bridge

Communicate with tools via postMessage (iframe/worker).

### listenForAgentCalls

Listen for tool calls from a client via postMessage.

```ts
import { listenForAgentCalls, signalCompletion } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const stopListening = listenForAgentCalls(async (toolName, args) => {
  // Execute the tool
  const result = await executeTool(toolName, args);
  // Signal the result
  signalCompletion(result);
});

// Later...
stopListening();
```

### callToolViaPostMessage

Call a tool in a remote context (worker/iframe) via postMessage.

```ts
import { callToolViaPostMessage } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const result = await callToolViaPostMessage(
  targetWindow,
  'compute',
  { a: 5, b: 3 }
);
```

### isWebMCPEvent

Check whether an event is a valid WebMCP message.

```ts
import { isWebMCPEvent } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

window.addEventListener('message', (e) => {
  if (isWebMCPEvent(e.data)) {
    // It is a WebMCP event
    console.log(e.data.type); // 'webmcp:call-tool', etc.
  }
});
```

## Full Example: Custom Server + Client

```ts
// === Server (backend) ===
import { createWebMcpServer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const server = createWebMcpServer('my-api', {
  description: 'API widgets',
});

server.addTool({
  name: 'fetch_data',
  description: 'Fetch data',
  inputSchema: {
    type: 'object',
    properties: {
      endpoint: { type: 'string' },
    },
    required: ['endpoint'],
  },
  execute: async (params) => {
    const { endpoint } = params as { endpoint: string };
    const response = await fetch(`/api/${endpoint}`);
    return await response.json();
  },
});

server.registerWidget(`
---
widget: data-display
description: Data display
schema:
  type: object
  properties:
    items:
      type: array
---
`, (container, data) => {
  const items = data.items as any[];
  container.innerHTML = items.map(i => `<div>${i}</div>`).join('');
});

// === Client (agent) ===
import { runAgentLoop } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const result = await runAgentLoop('Show the users', {
  provider: llmProvider,
  layers: [server.layer()],
  callbacks: {
    onToolCall: (call) => console.log(`Tool: ${call.name}`),
  },
});
```

<file path="src/content/docs/en/packages/sdk.mdx">
---
title: "@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk"
description: "Application SDK: canvas store, HyperSkill encoding, skills registry."
sidebar:
  order: 3
---

The `@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk` package provides application state (canvas store), HyperSkill orchestration, and skills registration.

## Canvas Store

Reactive application state store for managing widgets, mode, MCP connection, and chat history.

### Accessing the Store

```ts
import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';
// OR (in Svelte)
import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk/canvas';
```

### State Getters/Setters

```ts
// Widgets
canvas.blocks: Widget[];                      // Read: widget list
canvas.addWidget(type, data): Widget;         // Add a widget
canvas.removeBlock(id): void;                 // Remove by ID
canvas.updateBlock(id, data): void;           // Update data
canvas.moveBlock(fromId, toId): void;         // Move widget
canvas.clearBlocks(): void;                   // Clear the canvas
canvas.setBlocks(widgets): void;              // Replace all

// Mode
canvas.mode: 'auto' | 'drag' | 'chat';
canvas.setMode(mode): void;

// LLM
canvas.llm: 'haiku' | 'sonnet' | 'gemma-e2b' | 'gemma-e4b';
canvas.setLlm(model): void;

// MCP
canvas.mcpUrl: string;
canvas.setMcpUrl(url): void;
canvas.mcpConnected: boolean;
canvas.mcpConnecting: boolean;
canvas.mcpName: string;
canvas.mcpTools: McpToolInfo[];
canvas.setMcpConnecting(bool): void;
canvas.setMcpConnected(connected, name?, tools?): void;
canvas.setMcpError(error): void;

// Chat
canvas.messages: ChatMsg[];
canvas.addMsg(role, content, thinking?): ChatMsg;
canvas.updateMsg(id, content, thinking?): void;
canvas.clearMessages(): void;

// Theme
canvas.themeOverrides: Record<string, string>;
canvas.setThemeOverrides(overrides): void;

// Metrics
canvas.blockCount: number;
canvas.isEmpty: boolean;
canvas.generating: boolean;
```

### Svelte Example

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';
</script>

<!-- Svelte 5 binding -->
<select bind:value={canvas.llm}>
  <option value="haiku">Haiku</option>
  <option value="sonnet">Sonnet</option>
</select>

<button onclick={() => {
  canvas.addWidget('stat', {
    label: 'Sales',
    value: '1000'
  })
}}>Add widget</button>

<div class="widgets">
  {#each canvas.blocks as widget (widget.id)}
    <WidgetRenderer type={widget.type} data={widget.data} />
  {/each}
</div>
```

### Reactivity

The store supports two reactivity models:

**1. Svelte 5 (runes):**

```ts
// canvas.svelte.ts - with $state/$derived
import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

let blocks = $derived(canvas.blocks);
let empty = $derived(canvas.isEmpty);
```

**2. Framework-agnostic (subscribe):**

```ts
// canvas.ts - useSyncExternalStore pattern
const unsubscribe = canvas.subscribe(() => {
  const snapshot = canvas.getSnapshot();
  console.log(snapshot.blocks);
});
```

## HyperSkill: Encoding/Decoding

The HyperSkill system allows encoding/decoding skill configurations into short, shareable URLs.

### Encode

Serialize a skill into a URL parameter (auto-compression if >6KB).

```ts
import { encodeHyperSkill } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

const skill = {
  meta: {
    title: 'My Skill',
    llm: 'sonnet',
    mcp: 'http://localhost:3000/mcp',
  },
  content: {
    blocks: [
      { type: 'stat', data: { label: 'Revenue', value: '$42k' } },
    ]
  }
};

const url = await encodeHyperSkill(skill, sourceUrl);
// https://example.com?hs=g_qs9K2w... (gzip if >6KB)
```

**HyperSkill interface:**

```ts
interface HyperSkill {
  meta: HyperSkillMeta;
  content: unknown;  // Arbitrary data (blocks, etc.)
}

interface HyperSkillMeta {
  title?: string;
  description?: string;
  version?: string;
  created?: string;
  mcp?: string;
  mcpName?: string;
  llm?: string;
  tags?: string[];
  theme?: Record<string, string>;
  hash?: string;
  previousHash?: string;
  chatSummary?: string;
  provenance?: {
    mcpServers?: string[];
    toolsUsed?: string[];
    toolCallCount?: number;
    skillsReferenced?: string[];
    llm?: string;
    exportedAt?: string;
  };
}
```

### Decode

Parse a HyperSkill URL into a skill object.

```ts
import { decodeHyperSkill } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

const skill = await decodeHyperSkill(urlOrParam);
// { meta: {...}, content: {...} }
```

Automatically supports:
- Gzip compression (`gz.` prefix)
- Brotli compression (`br.` prefix)
- Plain Base64
- `?hs=...` parameter

### Hash & Versioning

Create a hashed version for version control.

```ts
import { computeHash, createVersion } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

const hash = await computeHash(sourceUrl, skillContent);
// "c7d3e2a1f4..."

const version = await createVersion(skill, sourceUrl, previousHash);
// { hash, previousHash, timestamp, skill }
```

### Diff

Compare two skill versions.

```ts
import { diffSkills } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

const changes = await diffSkills(oldSkill, newSkill);
// { added: [...], modified: [...], removed: [...] }
```

## Canvas Store x HyperSkill

Direct integration of the canvas store with HyperSkill:

```ts
import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

// Export the current configuration
const skill = canvas.buildSkillJSON();
// {
//   version: '1.0',
//   name: 'skill-...',
//   created: '2024-01-15T...',
//   mcp: canvas.mcpUrl,
//   llm: canvas.llm,
//   blocks: canvas.blocks.map(b => ({type, data})),
//   theme: canvas.themeOverrides
// }

// Generate a short HyperSkill URL
const param = await canvas.buildHyperskillParam();
// "g_qs9K2wZqE..." (compressed)

const url = `https://demos.hyperskills.net?hs=${param}`;

// Load from a parameter
await canvas.loadFromParam(param);

// Or from a full URL
await canvas.loadFromUrl(url);
```

## Skills Registry

Manage a collection of skills in localStorage + API.

### Registry API

```ts
import {
  createSkill,
  updateSkill,
  deleteSkill,
  getSkill,
  listSkills,
  clearSkills,
  loadSkills,
  onSkillsChange,
} from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

// Types
interface Skill {
  id: string;
  name: string;
  description?: string;
  content: any;
  created: number;
  updated: number;
  version?: string;
  tags?: string[];
}

interface SkillBlock {
  type: string;
  data: Record<string, unknown>;
}

// CRUD
const skill = createSkill('my-skill', {
  description: 'My awesome skill',
  content: { blocks: [...] },
});

updateSkill(skill.id, { name: 'New Name' });
deleteSkill(skill.id);
const retrieved = getSkill(skill.id);
const all = listSkills();

// Batch
await loadSkills(skillObjects);
clearSkills();

// Reactivity
onSkillsChange((skills) => {
  console.log('Skills changed:', skills);
});
```

### Example: Auto-Save

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';
  import { createSkill, updateSkill, listSkills } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

  let currentSkillId: string | null = null;

  function autoSave() {
    const skill = canvas.buildSkillJSON();
    if (!currentSkillId) {
      const created = createSkill(`skill_${Date.now()}`, skill);
      currentSkillId = created.id;
    } else {
      updateSkill(currentSkillId, skill);
    }
  }

  function loadAll() {
    return listSkills();
  }

  // Save every 5s if modified
  $effect(() => {
    canvas.blocks; // Dependency
    const timer = setTimeout(autoSave, 5000);
    return () => clearTimeout(timer);
  });
</script>

<div>
  <button onclick={autoSave}>Save</button>
  <button onclick={() => {
    const skills = loadAll();
    skills.forEach(s => console.log(s.name));
  }}>List skills</button>
</div>
```

## MCP Demo Servers

List available MCP demo servers.

```ts
import { MCP_DEMO_SERVERS } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';

interface McpDemoServer {
  name: string;
  description: string;
  url: string;
  tools: string[];
}

MCP_DEMO_SERVERS.forEach(server => {
  console.log(`${server.name}: ${server.url}`);
  console.log(`Tools: ${server.tools.join(', ')}`);
});
```

## Full Example: Multi-Skills Application

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';
  import { listSkills, createSkill, getSkill } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk';
  import { WidgetRenderer, LLMSelector } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/ui';

  let skills = listSkills();
  let selectedSkillId: string | null = null;

  async function selectSkill(id: string) {
    selectedSkillId = id;
    const skill = getSkill(id);
    if (skill?.content?.blocks) {
      canvas.setBlocks(skill.content.blocks);
    }
    if (skill?.content?.llm) {
      canvas.llm = skill.content.llm;
    }
  }

  function saveAsNew() {
    const skill = canvas.buildSkillJSON();
    const created = createSkill(
      `skill_${Date.now()}`,
      skill
    );
    skills = listSkills();
    selectedSkillId = created.id;
  }
</script>

<div class="flex h-screen">
  <!-- Sidebar: Skills list -->
  <aside class="w-64 p-4 bg-gray-100">
    <h2 class="font-bold mb-4">Skills</h2>
    <ul>
      {#each skills as skill (skill.id)}
        <li class="mb-2">
          <button
            class:selected={selectedSkillId === skill.id}
            onclick={() => selectSkill(skill.id)}
          >
            {skill.name}
          </button>
        </li>
      {/each}
    </ul>
    <button onclick={saveAsNew}>New skill</button>
  </aside>

  <!-- Main: Canvas + Controls -->
  <main class="flex-1 flex flex-col">
    <div class="p-4 border-b flex gap-4">
      <LLMSelector bind:value={canvas.llm} />
    </div>
    <div class="flex-1 p-4 overflow-auto">
      <div class="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4">
        {#each canvas.blocks as widget (widget.id)}
          <WidgetRenderer
            id={widget.id}
            type={widget.type}
            data={widget.data}
          />
        {/each}
      </div>
    </div>
  </main>
</div>

<style>
  button.selected {
    @apply bg-blue-500 text-white;
  }
</style>
```
</file>

<file path="src/content/docs/en/tutorials/architecture-mcp-webmcp.mdx">
---
title: MCP / WebMCP Architecture
description: Understand the symmetry between MCP (remote data) and WebMCP (local display), and how the agent loop orchestrates them
sidebar:
  order: 4
---

This tutorial explains how MCP and WebMCP coexist in webmcp-auto-ui, and how the agent loop orchestrates them transparently.

## The two protocols

The system relies on two symmetric protocols:

- **MCP** (Model Context Protocol) provides **remote data** -- SQL queries, REST APIs, scraping, etc.
- **WebMCP** provides **local display** -- widgets, canvas, browser interactions.

Each exposes **tools** (atomic actions) and **recipes** (composition guides).

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph MCP ["MCP (remote data)"]
        direction TB
        M1["Transport: HTTP Streamable\n(JSON-RPC 2.0)"]
        M2["Execution: remote server"]
        M3["Tools: query_sql, fetch_document"]
    end

    subgraph WebMCP ["WebMCP (local display)"]
        direction TB
        W1["Transport: in-process JS calls"]
        W2["Execution: local browser"]
        W3["Tools: widget_display, canvas"]
    end

    LLM["LLM"] --> MCP
    LLM --> WebMCP
```

### Comparison table

| Dimension       | MCP                            | WebMCP                          |
|-----------------|--------------------------------|---------------------------------|
| Role            | Data, APIs, databases          | Display, interaction            |
| Transport       | HTTP Streamable / stdio        | In-process JS calls             |
| Execution       | Remote server                  | Local browser                   |
| Latency         | Network (50-500ms)             | Instant (&lt;1ms)                  |
| Example tools   | query_sql, fetch_document      | widget_display, canvas          |
| Recipes         | Describe the data              | Describe the presentation       |
| Package         | `@webmcp-auto-ui/core`        | `@webmcp-auto-ui/core`         |

---

## The symmetry

The fundamental design is **symmetry**: the LLM does not distinguish an MCP tool from a WebMCP tool. Both protocols expose the same interface:

- `search_recipes()` -- discover available recipes
- `get_recipe()` -- get the schema and instructions
- Specific tools -- execute actions

From the LLM's perspective, an MCP call and a WebMCP call follow the same cycle: discovery, schema reading, execution. Only the internal routing differs -- the agent loop dispatches to the correct server based on the prefix.

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    LLM["LLM"]
    LLM -->|"*_mcp_*"| MC["McpClient\n(HTTP)"]
    LLM -->|"*_webmcp_*"| WS["WebMcpServer\n(local JS)"]
    MC --> SD["Remote server"]
    WS --> NAV["Browser\n(widgets)"]
```

---

## Uniform prefixing

All tools follow the naming convention:

```
{serverName}_{protocol}_{toolName}
```

Concrete examples with multiple connected servers:

| Full prefixed tool                           | serverName    | protocol | toolName        |
|----------------------------------------------|---------------|----------|-----------------|
| `tricoteuses_mcp_query_sql`                  | tricoteuses   | mcp      | query_sql       |
| `tricoteuses_mcp_search_recipes`             | tricoteuses   | mcp      | search_recipes  |
| `datagouv_mcp_fetch_dataset`                 | datagouv      | mcp      | fetch_dataset   |
| `autoui_webmcp_widget_display`               | autoui        | webmcp   | widget_display  |
| `autoui_webmcp_search_recipes`               | autoui        | webmcp   | search_recipes  |
| `designkit_webmcp_widget_display`            | designkit     | webmcp   | widget_display  |

Routing in the agent loop parses this prefix with a regex:

```typescript
/^(.+?)_(mcp|webmcp)_(.+)$/
```

Then dispatches:
- `protocol === 'mcp'` --> `McpClient.callTool(toolName, params)`
- `protocol === 'webmcp'` --> `WebMcpServer.executeTool(toolName, params)`

This prefixing guarantees **no name collisions** even with 10 servers connected simultaneously.

---

## The dynamic system prompt

`buildSystemPrompt(layers)` generates a **recipe-driven** prompt adapted to the connected servers. The prompt enforces a strict 4-step workflow:

1. **Discovery** -- call `search_recipes()` to find the relevant recipe
2. **Reading** -- call `get_recipe()` to read the instructions
3. **Execution** -- follow the recipe instructions (fetch data, etc.)
4. **Display** -- use `widget_display`, `canvas`, `recall` for UI rendering

### Dynamic placeholders

The tool lists at steps 1, 2, and 4 are **placeholders**: `buildSystemPrompt` automatically injects the prefixed names based on the connected layers. With 2 MCP servers and 1 WebMCP, step 1 will contain for example:

```
tricoteuses_mcp_search_recipes(), datagouv_mcp_search_recipes(), autoui_webmcp_search_recipes()
```

### Per-app customization

Apps can pass a custom `systemPrompt` in the `runAgentLoop()` options. When provided, it replaces the generated prompt. However, the unified prompt adapts to the connected servers and covers the majority of cases.

---

## Lazy loading

At startup, the agent loop does **not** expose all tools from all servers. It only provides discovery tools:

| Protocol | Tools exposed at start                               |
|----------|------------------------------------------------------|
| MCP      | `search_recipes`, `get_recipe`                       |
| WebMCP   | `search_recipes`, `get_recipe`, `widget_display`,    |
|          | `canvas`, `recall`                                   |

WebMCP action tools (`widget_display`, `canvas`, `recall`) are always present because they are needed to display results.

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant LLM
    participant Loop as Agent Loop
    participant MCP as MCP Server

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 1 - Discovery
    LLM->>Loop: tricoteuses_mcp_search_recipes("profile")
    Loop->>MCP: callTool("search_recipes", ...)
    MCP-->>Loop: [{name: "parl-profile"}]
    Note over Loop: activateServerTools(tricoteuses)
    Note over Loop: All MCP tools now active

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 2 - Data
    LLM->>Loop: tricoteuses_mcp_query_sql(...)
    Loop->>MCP: callTool("query_sql", ...)
    MCP-->>Loop: {name: "Dupont", ...}
```

When the LLM calls a tool from a server for the first time, `activateServerTools()` adds all tools from that server to the active set. The server is activated only once.

### Token savings

With 4 servers and 50 tools total, discovery mode exposes about 20 tools instead of 50. This represents savings of approximately 3,000-5,000 tokens in the initial prompt -- significant when the budget is 8K tokens per turn.

---

## The schema pipeline

Widget schemas follow a 4-step pipeline, from Svelte component to runtime:

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    A["Svelte component\ninterface Props"] --> B["sync-schemas.ts\nParse TS -> JSON Schema\nInject into frontmatter"]
    B --> C["Recipe .md\nwidget: stat\nschema: ..."]
    C --> D["WebMCP Server\nregisterWidget()\nparse frontmatter\nvalidate params"]
```

The `sync-schemas.ts` script maintains an explicit mapping between each widget name and its `.svelte` file (e.g. `"stat"` ↔ `StatBlock.svelte`, `"profile"` ↔ `ProfileCard.svelte`).

### Runtime validation

When the LLM calls `widget_display(name, params)`, the WebMCP server validates the params against the JSON Schema **before** passing them to the renderer:

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    A["LLM calls\nwidget_display('stat', params)"] --> B{"validateJsonSchema\n(params, schema)"}
    B -->|valid| C["Returns\n{widget: 'stat', data: params, id: 'w_x'}"]
    B -->|invalid| D["Returns\n{error: 'Validation failed',\ndetails: [...],\nexpected_schema: {...}}"]
    D --> E["LLM corrects its params\nand retries"]
    C --> F["WidgetRenderer\nStatBlock.svelte"]
```

If validation fails, the LLM receives an error message with the expected schema, allowing it to correct its call.

---

## Full conversation flow

Sequence diagram of a typical conversation. The user asks: "Show me the profile of MP Jean Dupont".

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant U as User
    participant LLM
    participant Loop as Agent Loop
    participant MCP as MCP Server
    participant WS as WebMCP Server

    U->>LLM: "Profile of Jean Dupont"

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 1 - Discovery
    LLM->>Loop: tricoteuses_mcp_search_recipes("profile")
    Loop->>MCP: callTool("search_recipes", ...)
    MCP-->>Loop: [{name: "parl-profile", desc: "..."}]
    Note over Loop: activateServerTools(tricoteuses)
    Loop-->>LLM: result

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 2 - Data
    LLM->>Loop: tricoteuses_mcp_query_sql("SELECT ... mp")
    Loop->>MCP: callTool("query_sql", ...)
    MCP-->>Loop: {name: "Dupont", group: "RE", photo: "..."}
    Loop-->>LLM: result

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 3 - Schema
    LLM->>Loop: autoui_webmcp_get_recipe("profile")
    Loop->>WS: executeTool("get_recipe", ...)
    WS-->>Loop: {schema: {...}, recipe: "..."}
    Loop-->>LLM: result

    Note over LLM,Loop: Iteration 4 - Display
    LLM->>Loop: autoui_webmcp_widget_display("profile", {...})
    Loop->>WS: executeTool("widget_display", ...)
    WS-->>Loop: {widget: "profile", data: {...}, id: "w_x"}
    Note over Loop: onWidget() -> WidgetRenderer -> ProfileCard
    Loop-->>LLM: result

    LLM-->>U: "Here is the profile of Jean Dupont"
    Note over U: ProfileCard rendered on the canvas
```

### Safety mechanisms

Two safeguards prevent infinite loops:

1. **Iterations without rendering counter** -- after 4 iterations without `widget_display`, discovery tools are removed from the active set. After 5 iterations, a nudge message is injected.

2. **`maxIterations`** (default 5) -- the loop stops even if the LLM has not finished.

### Result compression

After each iteration, previous `tool_result` entries are compressed: texts longer than 300 characters are truncated to 200 with a `recall('id')` hint. The LLM can retrieve the full result via the `recall` tool.

---

## Multi-server

Multiple MCP and WebMCP servers coexist thanks to uniform prefixing.

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph Loop ["Agent Loop"]
        direction TB
        SP["buildSystemPrompt(layers)"]
        DT["buildDiscoveryTools(layers)"]
        AS["activateServerTools()"]
    end

    subgraph MCP ["MCP Layers"]
        M1["tricoteuses\nprotocol: mcp\ntools: query_sql, search_recipes, ..."]
        M2["datagouv\nprotocol: mcp\ntools: fetch_dataset, ..."]
    end

    subgraph WebMCP ["WebMCP Layers"]
        W1["autoui\nprotocol: webmcp\n26 native widgets"]
        W2["designkit\nprotocol: webmcp\ndesign widgets"]
    end

    Loop --> MCP
    Loop --> WebMCP
```

### Namespace isolation

Each server is a complete namespace. If `autoui` and `designkit` both expose a `widget_display` tool, the LLM sees:

- `autoui_webmcp_widget_display` -- standard widgets (stat, chart, map...)
- `designkit_webmcp_widget_display` -- design widgets (mockup, wireframe...)

No possible confusion.

---

## The canonical resolver (4 layers)

MCP servers do not always use the exact names `search_recipes` and `get_recipe`. The canonical resolver identifies equivalent tools via 4 matching layers:

| Layer   | Strategy | Example |
|---------|----------|---------|
| Layer 1 | Exact name match | `search_recipes` |
| Layer 2 | Decomposition (action, resource) | `list_skills` --> action=list, resource=skills --> search_recipes |
| Layer 3 | Description scan for keywords | description contains "recipe" + action "search" |
| Layer 4 | Fallback: no recipe tool, list raw tools | server without recipes |

The resolver registers **aliases** in a local map:

```typescript
// If the server exposes "list_skills" instead of "search_recipes"
aliasMap.set('server_mcp_search_recipes', 'server_mcp_list_skills');
```

The system prompt uses the canonical name (`search_recipes`), and the agent loop resolves the alias at execution time.

---

## Extensibility

The layer-based architecture is designed to accommodate new server types without modifying the agent loop.

### Browser WebMCP

A `browser` WebMCP server could expose `notify`, `clipboard`, `share`, `download`. The LLM would call `browser_webmcp_notify(...)`.

### Native WebMCP (SwiftUI bridge)

A native bridge could expose `widget_display` (SwiftUI rendering), `haptic`, `speech`. Same convention: `native_webmcp_*`.

### New protocols

`ToolLayer` is a discriminated union by `protocol`. Adding a third type = new union member + a case in `buildToolsFromLayers()`.

```typescript
// Today
export type ToolLayer = McpLayer | WebMcpLayer;
// Tomorrow
export type ToolLayer = McpLayer | WebMcpLayer | WasmLayer;
```

---

## Overall architecture

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph Browser ["BROWSER"]
        APP["App (SvelteKit)\nChat, Config, Canvas"]
        LOOP["Agent Loop\nLLM provider, Tool dispatch\nLazy loading, Compression"]
        BR["WidgetRenderer\nDispatch: type -> widget\ndata -> props"]
        WS["WebMCP Server(s)\nautoui, designkit, ..."]
        PROV["LLM Provider\nRemote / Wasm / Local"]

        APP --> LOOP
        LOOP --> BR
        LOOP --> WS
        LOOP --> PROV
    end

    subgraph Remote ["REMOTE SERVERS"]
        MCPS["MCP Server(s)\ntricoteuses, datagouv"]
        LLMAPI["LLM API\nClaude, Ollama"]
    end

    LOOP -->|"MCP Streamable HTTP"| MCPS
    PROV -->|"HTTP"| LLMAPI
```

---

## Summary

| Concept                | Implementation                                |
|------------------------|-----------------------------------------------|
| Protocols              | MCP (remote) + WebMCP (local), symmetric      |
| Prefixing              | `{server}_{protocol}_{tool}`                  |
| Layers                 | `McpLayer[]` + `WebMcpLayer[]` = `ToolLayer[]`|
| Lazy loading           | `buildDiscoveryTools()` + `activateServerTools()` |
| System prompt          | `buildSystemPrompt(layers)` -- dynamic        |
| Schema pipeline        | TS Props --> sync-schemas --> .md --> WebMCP   |
| Validation             | JSON Schema at runtime before rendering       |
| Multi-server           | Isolated namespaces, aliases, recipe filtering |
| Canonical resolver     | 4 layers: exact, decomposition, description, fallback |
| Context compression    | Truncation + recall() for long results        |
| Extensibility          | Discriminated union `ToolLayer`, new type      |

## See also

- [Getting started with the boilerplate](./boilerplate)
- [Create a WebMCP server](./create-webmcp-server)
- [System architecture](/guide/architecture)
</file>

<file path="src/content/docs/en/tutorials/boilerplate.mdx">
---
title: Getting started with the boilerplate
description: Install the Svelte 5 / SvelteKit / shadcn-svelte boilerplate and connect webmcp-auto-ui in 10 minutes
sidebar:
  order: 0
---

This tutorial walks you step by step through installing the webmcp-auto-ui boilerplate, connecting to an MCP server, and creating your first custom widget.

## Overview

The boilerplate provides a SvelteKit 5 app pre-wired with:

- **shadcn-svelte** for the design system
- **@webmcp-auto-ui/core** for the MCP client and WebMCP server
- **@webmcp-auto-ui/agent** for the agent loop and LLM provider
- **@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk** for the canvas store and HyperSkill encoding
- **@webmcp-auto-ui/ui** for components (LLMSelector, McpStatus, WidgetRenderer, etc.)

The app includes 3 custom widgets (MP profiles, ballots, amendments) as integration examples.

---

## Step 1: Scaffolding

Clone the boilerplate with degit:

```bash
npx degit hyperskills/webmcp-auto-ui/apps/boilerplate my-app
cd my-app
npm install
```

---

## Step 2: Configure the API proxy

Create the file `src/routes/api/chat/+server.ts` (already present in the boilerplate):

```ts
import { env } from '$env/dynamic/private';
import type { RequestHandler } from '@sveltejs/kit';
import { anthropicProxy } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent/server';

export const POST: RequestHandler = async ({ request }) => {
  const body = await request.json() as Record<string, unknown>;
  const apiKey = (body.__apiKey as string | undefined) || env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY || '';
  delete body.__apiKey;
  return anthropicProxy(body, apiKey, request.headers.get('X-Model'));
};
```

Add your API key in `.env`:

```
ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-...
```

The proxy relays requests to the Claude API. The model is selected dynamically via the `X-Model` header (aliases: `'haiku'`, `'sonnet'`, `'opus'`).

---

## Step 3: Connect an MCP server

The boilerplate uses `McpMultiClient` to manage multiple MCP servers:

```ts
import { McpMultiClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const multiClient = new McpMultiClient();
await multiClient.addServer('https://mcp.code4code.eu/mcp');
```

In the main component, the connection is already wired with a URL field and a "Connect" button. On page load, the app automatically connects to the default URL.

To hardcode a server:

```ts
await multiClient.addServer('https://your-mcp-server.example/mcp');
```

---

## Step 4: Understand the LLM provider

The boilerplate uses `RemoteLLMProvider` to communicate with Claude via the proxy:

```ts
import { RemoteLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const provider = new RemoteLLMProvider({ proxyUrl: '/api/chat' });
```

The model is changed dynamically via the `<LLMSelector>` component which exposes the aliases `'haiku'`, `'sonnet'` and `'opus'`.

---

## Step 5: Run the agent loop

The agent loop orchestrates the LLM, MCP tools and WebMCP widgets:

```ts
import { runAgentLoop, buildSystemPrompt, fromMcpTools, autoui } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import type { ToolLayer, McpLayer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

// Build layers (remote MCP + local WebMCP)
const layers: ToolLayer[] = [];

// MCP layer (remote data)
for (const server of multiClient.listServers()) {
  const mcpLayer: McpLayer = {
    protocol: 'mcp',
    serverName: server.name,
    tools: fromMcpTools(server.tools),
  };
  layers.push(mcpLayer);
}

// WebMCP layer (native widgets)
layers.push(autoui.layer());

// Dynamic system prompt
const systemPrompt = buildSystemPrompt(layers);

// Run the loop
const result = await runAgentLoop(userMessage, {
  provider,
  systemPrompt,
  layers,
  maxIterations: 10,
  maxTokens: 4096,
  callbacks: {
    onWidget: (type, data) => {
      // Add the widget to the canvas
      const id = 'b_' + Date.now().toString(36);
      blocks = [...blocks, { id, type, data }];
      return { id };
    },
    onText: (text) => { ephemeralText = text; },
    onToolCall: (call) => { console.log('Tool:', call.name); },
  },
});
```

---

## Step 6: Display widgets

Widget rendering is done via `<WidgetRenderer>`:

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { WidgetRenderer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/ui';
</script>

<div class="grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-2 gap-4">
  {#each blocks as block (block.id)}
    <WidgetRenderer
      id={block.id}
      type={block.type}
      data={block.data}
      {servers}
    />
  {/each}
</div>
```

`WidgetRenderer` automatically resolves the Svelte component matching the widget `type`, by looking in:
1. Custom WebMCP servers (passed via `servers`)
2. Native autoui widgets (stat, chart, table, map, etc.)

---

## Step 7: Add UI components

The boilerplate integrates pre-built UI components:

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import {
    LLMSelector,     // Model selector (haiku/sonnet/opus)
    McpStatus,       // MCP connection indicator
    AgentProgress,   // Agent loop progress
    WidgetRenderer,  // Widget rendering
    getTheme,        // Light/dark theme
  } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/ui';
</script>

<!-- Top bar -->
<header class="flex items-center gap-3 px-4 border-b">
  <McpStatus
    connecting={canvas.mcpConnecting}
    connected={canvas.mcpConnected}
    name={mcpName}
    servers={multiClient.listServers().map(s => ({
      url: s.url, name: s.name, toolCount: s.tools.length
    }))}
  />
  <LLMSelector />
</header>

<!-- Agent progress -->
<AgentProgress
  active={canvas.generating}
  elapsed={chatTimer}
  toolCalls={chatToolCount}
  lastTool={chatLastTool}
/>
```

---

## Step 8: Add a custom widget

To register your own widgets, create a local WebMCP server:

```ts
import { createWebMcpServer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';
import MyWidget from './widgets/MyWidget.svelte';
import myWidgetRecipe from './recipes/my-widget.md?raw';

const myServer = createWebMcpServer('my-app', {
  description: 'Custom widgets for my application',
});

myServer.registerWidget(myWidgetRecipe, MyWidget);
```

Then add the layer to the agent loop:

```ts
layers.push(myServer.layer());
```

And pass the server to WidgetRenderer:

```svelte
<WidgetRenderer
  id={block.id}
  type={block.type}
  data={block.data}
  servers={[myServer]}
/>
```

For details on creating custom widgets, see the tutorial [Create a custom widget](./create-custom-widget).

---

## Start the development server

```bash
npm run dev
```

The app is accessible at `http://localhost:5173`. Type a question in the chat to trigger the agent loop.

---

## Project structure

```
my-app/
  src/
    routes/
      +page.svelte          # Main page (chat + canvas)
      api/chat/+server.ts   # Claude API proxy
    lib/
      widgets/
        register.ts         # WebMCP server + widget registration
        MyWidget.svelte     # Custom widget component
      recipes/
        my-widget.md        # Widget recipe (frontmatter + instructions)
  .env                      # ANTHROPIC_API_KEY
  package.json
  svelte.config.js
  vite.config.ts
```

<file path="src/content/docs/en/tutorials/connect-mcp-server.mdx">
---
title: Connect an MCP server
description: Integrate an external MCP server and use its tools in the agent
sidebar:
  order: 3
---

This tutorial shows how to connect an **external MCP server** (Model Context Protocol) and integrate it with the agent loop to execute tools remotely.

## Key concepts

**MCP** (Model Context Protocol) is a client-server protocol that allows an LLM to access remote tools:

```mermaid
graph LR
    A["Agent<br/>runAgentLoop()"]
    B["MCP Client<br/>McpClient"]
    C["MCP Server<br/>(remote data)"]
    D["Exposed tools<br/>(API, DB)"]

    A -->|Calls tool| B
    B -->|JSON-RPC via HTTP| C
    C -->|Executes| D
```

## Step 1: Initialize the MCP client

```typescript
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

const mcpClient = new McpClient('http://localhost:3000/mcp', {
  clientName: 'WebMCP Auto-UI',
  clientVersion: '1.0.0',
  timeout: 30000,
});

// Initialize the connection
await mcpClient.initialize();

// Retrieve the list of available tools
const tools = await mcpClient.listTools();
console.log('Available tools:', tools);
```

## Step 2: Create a tool layer (ToolLayer)

A `ToolLayer` encapsulates an MCP server with its tools in the format expected by the agent:

```typescript
import type { ToolLayer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

// Retrieve server tools
async function createMcpLayer(): Promise<ToolLayer> {
  const client = new McpClient('https://api.example.com/mcp');
  await client.initialize();

  const tools = await client.listTools();

  return {
    protocol: 'mcp',
    serverName: 'example-api',
    description: 'Tools for accessing the Example API',
    serverUrl: 'https://api.example.com/mcp',
    tools: tools.map(t => ({
      name: t.name,
      description: t.description ?? '',
      inputSchema: t.inputSchema,
    })),
  };
}

// Create the layer
const exampleLayer = await createMcpLayer();
```

## Step 3: Integrate with the agent loop

Pass the MCP client and tool layers to `runAgentLoop()`:

```typescript
import { runAgentLoop } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { RemoteLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

const provider = new RemoteLLMProvider({
  proxyUrl: '/api/chat',
  model: 'sonnet',  // resolves to claude-sonnet-4-6
});

const result = await runAgentLoop('Search for articles about Svelte', {
  client: mcpClient,  // <-- Pass the MCP client
  provider,
  layers: [exampleLayer],  // <-- Pass the tool layers
  maxIterations: 5,
  callbacks: {
    onToolCall: (call) => {
      console.log(`Tool called: ${call.name}`);
      if (call.result) console.log('Result:', call.result);
      if (call.error) console.log('Error:', call.error);
    },
    onText: (text) => {
      console.log('Agent says:', text);
    },
  },
});
```

## Full example: Connect a Wikipedia API

```typescript
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';
import { runAgentLoop } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { RemoteLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import type { ToolLayer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

async function queryWikipedia(topic: string) {
  // Initialize the MCP client pointing to a Wikipedia server
  const client = new McpClient('https://mcp-wikipedia.example.com');
  await client.initialize();

  // Create the tool layer
  const tools = await client.listTools();
  const wikiLayer: ToolLayer = {
    protocol: 'mcp',
    serverName: 'wikipedia',
    description: 'Access to Wikipedia',
    tools: tools.map(t => ({
      name: t.name,
      description: t.description ?? '',
      inputSchema: t.inputSchema,
    })),
  };

  // Initialize the LLM
  const provider = new RemoteLLMProvider({
    proxyUrl: '/api/chat',
    model: 'sonnet',
  });

  // Run the agent loop
  const result = await runAgentLoop(
    `Retrieve detailed information about: ${topic}`,
    {
      client,
      provider,
      layers: [wikiLayer],
      maxIterations: 5,
      callbacks: {
        onToolCall: (call) => {
          console.log(`[${call.name}]`, call.args);
        },
        onText: (text) => {
          console.log('>', text);
        },
        onDone: (metrics) => {
          console.log(`Done in ${metrics.totalTokens} tokens`);
        },
      },
    }
  );

  return result.text;
}

// Usage
const answer = await queryWikipedia('French Revolution');
console.log(answer);
```

## Step 4: Handle multiple MCP servers

You can combine multiple MCP servers in a single agent session:

```typescript
async function createMultiServerSetup() {
  // Server 1: Data API
  const dataClient = new McpClient('https://api.data.example.com/mcp');
  await dataClient.initialize();
  const dataTools = await dataClient.listTools();
  const dataLayer: ToolLayer = {
    protocol: 'mcp',
    serverName: 'data-api',
    description: 'Data access',
    tools: dataTools.map(t => ({
      name: t.name,
      description: t.description ?? '',
      inputSchema: t.inputSchema,
    })),
  };

  // Server 2: Search
  const searchClient = new McpClient('https://search.example.com/mcp');
  await searchClient.initialize();
  const searchTools = await searchClient.listTools();
  const searchLayer: ToolLayer = {
    protocol: 'mcp',
    serverName: 'search-engine',
    description: 'Search engine',
    tools: searchTools.map(t => ({
      name: t.name,
      description: t.description ?? '',
      inputSchema: t.inputSchema,
    })),
  };

  // Run the agent with both servers
  return await runAgentLoop(
    'Find and analyze the latest trends',
    {
      client: dataClient,  // Use the primary client
      provider: new RemoteLLMProvider({ /* ... */ }),
      layers: [dataLayer, searchLayer],  // Combine layers
      maxIterations: 10,
    }
  );
}
```

## Error handling

```typescript
async function safeConnectMcp(url: string) {
  try {
    const client = new McpClient(url, {
      timeout: 10000,
      autoReconnect: true,
      maxReconnectAttempts: 3,
    });

    await client.initialize();
    console.log('Connection established');
    return client;
  } catch (error) {
    if (error instanceof Error) {
      if (error.message.includes('timeout')) {
        console.error('MCP server unreachable (timeout)');
      } else if (error.message.includes('404')) {
        console.error('MCP endpoint not found');
      } else {
        console.error('Connection error:', error.message);
      }
    }
    return null;
  }
}

// Usage
const client = await safeConnectMcp('https://api.example.com/mcp');
if (client) {
  // Continue with the client
}
```

## Lazy loading tools

For servers with many tools, use lazy loading with `buildDiscoveryTools`:

```typescript
import { buildDiscoveryTools, activateServerTools } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';

// First create the discovery layer (lightweight tools)
const discoveryTools = buildDiscoveryTools([mcpLayer]);

// Pass to runAgentLoop
const result = await runAgentLoop('...', {
  client: mcpClient,
  provider,
  layers: [mcpLayer],
  // Full tools will be activated on demand
});

// Internally, the agent will activate full tools when a tool from this server is called
```

## Pattern: Agent loop with MCP in an API

```typescript
// api/agent/+server.ts
import { json } from '@sveltejs/kit';
import { runAgentLoop } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { RemoteLLMProvider } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/agent';
import { McpClient } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/core';

export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { message, mcpUrl } = await request.json();

  const mcpClient = new McpClient(mcpUrl);
  await mcpClient.initialize();

  const tools = await mcpClient.listTools();
  const layer = {
    protocol: 'mcp' as const,
    serverName: new URL(mcpUrl).hostname,
    description: 'MCP Server',
    tools: tools.map(t => ({
      name: t.name,
      description: t.description ?? '',
      inputSchema: t.inputSchema,
    })),
  };

  const result = await runAgentLoop(message, {
    client: mcpClient,
    provider: new RemoteLLMProvider({
      proxyUrl: '/api/chat',
      model: 'sonnet',
    }),
    layers: [layer],
    maxIterations: 5,
  });

  return json({
    text: result.text,
    toolCalls: result.toolCalls,
    metrics: result.metrics,
  });
}
```

## Integration with the Svelte UI

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { canvas } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/sdk/canvas';
  import { BlockRenderer } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/ui';
  import { AgentProgress } from '@webmcp-auto-ui/ui';

  let mcpUrl = 'https://api.example.com/mcp';
  let userMessage = '';
  let loading = false;

  async function runAgent() {
    if (!userMessage.trim()) return;

    loading = true;
    canvas.setGenerating(true);

    try {
      const response = await fetch('/api/agent', {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
        body: JSON.stringify({ message: userMessage, mcpUrl }),
      });

      const result = await response.json();

      // Add the result to the canvas
      canvas.addMsg('user', userMessage);
      canvas.addMsg('assistant', result.text);

      // Add generated widgets
      result.toolCalls.forEach((call: any) => {
        if (call.name.includes('widget_display')) {
          canvas.addWidget('json-viewer', {
            data: call.result,
          });
        }
      });

      userMessage = '';
    } catch (error) {
      console.error('Agent error:', error);
      canvas.addMsg('assistant', 'Error during execution');
    } finally {
      loading = false;
      canvas.setGenerating(false);
    }
  }
</script>

<div class="agent-panel">
  <input
    bind:value={mcpUrl}
    placeholder="MCP server URL"
    disabled={loading}
  />
  <textarea
    bind:value={userMessage}
    placeholder="Your question..."
    disabled={loading}
  />
  <button onclick={runAgent} disabled={loading}>
    {loading ? 'Processing...' : 'Send'}
  </button>

  {#if loading}
    <AgentProgress />
  {/if}

  <div class="results">
    {#each canvas.blocks as block (block.id)}
      <BlockRenderer id={block.id} type={block.type} data={block.data} />
    {/each}
  </div>
</div>

<style>
  .agent-panel {
    display: flex;
    flex-direction: column;
    gap: 1rem;
    padding: 1.5rem;
  }

  input, textarea {
    padding: 0.5rem;
    border: 1px solid #e5e7eb;
    border-radius: 0.375rem;
  }

  textarea {
    min-height: 80px;
    resize: vertical;
  }

  button:disabled {
    opacity: 0.5;
    cursor: not-allowed;
  }

  .results {
    display: grid;
    gap: 1rem;
  }
</style>
```

## Debugging

To inspect MCP calls in detail:

```typescript
// Add logging to the client
const client = new McpClient(url);

// Tool results are in AgentResult.toolCalls
const result = await runAgentLoop(message, {
  client,
  provider,
  layers,
  callbacks: {
    onToolCall: (call) => {
      console.log('=== TOOL CALL ===');
      console.log('Name:', call.name);
      console.log('Args:', JSON.stringify(call.args, null, 2));
      console.log('Result:', call.result);
      console.log('Duration:', call.elapsed, 'ms');
    },
  },
});
```
